  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b14875b0-f602-496e-a81d-c3b188d95dcf'

Wounded, unsure if he’ll walk agai</span>
  <span id="freeText13764136119627378692" style="display:none">Heroes come in many forms--soldiers who fall and rise, ordinary people doing extraordinary things, women who battle for their marriage, reporters who fight for truth and justice, and men who put it all on the line for the women they love.<br /><br />Sometimes heroes fall. <br /><br />Colonel Michael Cedars is a decorated war hero returning home from Afghanistan. Wounded, unsure if he’ll walk again, he’s not sure how he fits in civilian life, and he definitely questions if he wants to remain married to the feisty redhead, Hope Shane.<br /><br />Hope’s never been one to play it safe. She met the Colonel while working as a war correspondent, fell in love with the man in uniform, watched him get blown up, and isn’t willing to give up on him now. <br /><br />Back in Denver, Colorado, she’s working as an investigative reporter who becomes entangled in a human trafficking story. As the danger of her story intensifies, Hope and Michael are tested more than they ever imagined. Will Michael be able to see beyond what he’s lost to embrace what remains? Is he still the man she married or has he become a liability that could get her killed? Is he still the hero she claims him to be? Will her reckless pursuit of justice endanger the life they’ve pieced together?</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619964453?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/20524165-melissa">Melissa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619964453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17870432162501478688">I don't know where to begin...this book reached inside my heart, grabbed hold and refused to let go. Even now, after reading the words "the end", I'm still wanting more of Hope and Michael's story. It's a very different concept--at least from the books I can recall offhand. I loved the originality of the plot and the characters. I can see this as a movie--hint, hint to anyone out there listening! Hope is the kind of woman who would probably intimidate me in real life--at least at first--but she'</span>
  <span id="freeText17870432162501478688" style="display:none">I don't know where to begin...this book reached inside my heart, grabbed hold and refused to let go. Even now, after reading the words "the end", I'm still wanting more of Hope and Michael's story. It's a very different concept--at least from the books I can recall offhand. I loved the originality of the plot and the characters. I can see this as a movie--hint, hint to anyone out there listening! Hope is the kind of woman who would probably intimidate me in real life--at least at first--but she's also the kind of woman I'd be honored to call a friend. The back cover of this book talks about heroes--and that is a theme that carries throughout the book. This is a timely book--the issues are relevant to today's society--but it didn't feel pushed down our throats. The plot, the characters, the EMOTION blew my mind. This author has definitely made it onto my favorite author's list! I've just read all three of her books in two weeks--lol. I hope there's more to come because this reader is now a fan. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17870432162501478688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_728233353" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/728233353" />
    <a title="Christoph Fischer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13998364-christoph-fischer"><img alt="Christoph Fischer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473825343p2/13998364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/728233353?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christoph Fischer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christoph Fischer" href="/user/show/13998364-christoph-fischer">Christoph Fischer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer728233353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2637739462685206374">I was interested in “Reckless Endangerment” by Amber Lea Easton because of some of her non-fiction work that had quite impressed me and I wanted to see how her talent would show in a different genre.<br/>From the first page is was evident how well Easton can draw her readers into the story and how skilful she creates characters that we instantly will want to know more about. The wounded Afghanistan war veteran Michael and his journalist love interest Hope are far from one dimensional creations and th</span>
  <span id="freeText2637739462685206374" style="display:none">I was interested in “Reckless Endangerment” by Amber Lea Easton because of some of her non-fiction work that had quite impressed me and I wanted to see how her talent would show in a different genre.<br />From the first page is was evident how well Easton can draw her readers into the story and how skilful she creates characters that we instantly will want to know more about. The wounded Afghanistan war veteran Michael and his journalist love interest Hope are far from one dimensional creations and the problems they face in their strange relationship are much more gripping than a mere ‘taming-of-the-shrew’ scenario. Both characters have a lot to keep you interested in them and make you want them to succeed and grow. <br />Although this book is marketed as romantic suspense it also covers some serious issues, such as people trafficking and post-traumatic stress disorder, adding further depth to a book that is rich in plot and personal conflict already. Nothing prepared me for the literary quality of this novel. Regular romance and suspense fans get more than enough here to be satisfied by the great chemistry between the main characters and the intriguing story lines. However, if you – like myself – want a little bit more out of a book than you will find it in the well-handled and insightful passages about trafficking and PSD, issues that are handled with care rather than in an exploitative or decorative manner. <br />Easton clearly cares about what she writes and it pays dividends, her book is surprisingly impressive and certainly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2637739462685206374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12790510837529042301" style="display:none">I'm not very good at writing reviews, but I highly recommend this novel so am giving it my best shot. From the first moment, when the reader meets Colonel Michael Cedars, it's obvious that this is going to be a deeper novel than the typical romantic suspense. It deals with a wounded marine (Michael) and his wife (Hope) who is an investigative reporter involved in a human trafficking story in Colorado. All I can really say is--WOW. This novel blew me away--I even cried at times, becoming so involved with the emotional journey the characters go on--and laughed--and really rooted for them all through the book. I love romantic suspense novels, have read one other from this author that prompted me to read this one (Riptide--LOVE THE ENDING), and am definitely going to look for more from this author. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17137698857829328139">Fabulous novel! I didn't want it to end. I started out reading the prequel that the author posted on her website (yes, I'm a fan) so was hooked before reading page one of this new release. The storyline was unexpected...which is refreshing to find in a romantic suspense novel. The story and the characters feel like they've been ripped from the news. Riveting. I liked that the hero (a war vet from Afghanistan, a marine) is partially paralyzed, yet written about as the sexy, smart guy he is. And t</span>
  <span id="freeText17137698857829328139" style="display:none">Fabulous novel! I didn't want it to end. I started out reading the prequel that the author posted on her website (yes, I'm a fan) so was hooked before reading page one of this new release. The storyline was unexpected...which is refreshing to find in a romantic suspense novel. The story and the characters feel like they've been ripped from the news. Riveting. I liked that the hero (a war vet from Afghanistan, a marine) is partially paralyzed, yet written about as the sexy, smart guy he is. And the heroine--I'd like to have a beer with her sometime. She's the kind of heroine that you root for, cry for, and really feel for throughout the story. The couple is perfect together--their love story feels authentic and bigger than life. They're both heroes...and what a great idea for a story. I'm sure I will read this again and again in the future, it's that kind of story. Once again, this author delivered a blockbuster story that deserves to see the big screen one day. I highly recommend. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1790855237175224891">Excellent read, great character development, exciting plot--buy it! You won't be disappointed with this novel. Like I said, you won't be disappointed, this is </span>
  <span id="freeText1790855237175224891" style="display:none">Excellent read, great character development, exciting plot--buy it! You won't be disappointed with this novel. The author did a great job handling the PTSD and physical challenges of the story without being overt about it--I mean, not overly "in your face". From the first page, I felt intensely connected to the characters and was pulled into the suspense plot. Great romantic suspense novel, touching love story, and very well done across the board. Like I said, you won't be disappointed, this is a definite "must own" to re-read every now and then. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1790855237175224891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_659731994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/659731994" />
    <a title="Jody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1037305-jody"><img alt="Jody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242570762p2/1037305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/659731994?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody" href="/user/show/1037305-jody">Jody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer659731994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11954938152924392795">By the end of Reckless Endangerment I can sum it up by saying it's Triple-H......heartbreaking, heartwarming, and heartpounding. It's full of likable and fully fleshed-out characters, realistically depicted issues related to the aftermath of war, and it presented a fast-paced mystery surrounding human trafficking that kept me on the edge of my seat. It shows that atrocities not only occur in faraway lands but outside our front door as well. As two people deal both mentally and physically with th</span>
  <span id="freeText11954938152924392795" style="display:none">By the end of Reckless Endangerment I can sum it up by saying it's Triple-H......heartbreaking, heartwarming, and heartpounding. It's full of likable and fully fleshed-out characters, realistically depicted issues related to the aftermath of war, and it presented a fast-paced mystery surrounding human trafficking that kept me on the edge of my seat. It shows that atrocities not only occur in faraway lands but outside our front door as well. As two people deal both mentally and physically with the hand war dealt them it's only through love and acceptance that true healing can begin and a HEA can be fully achieved.<br /><br />Hope Shane gives the impression of being a total badass who can handle any situation. She loves being in the thick of things and is totally dedicated to the causes and few people she cares about. Some might call her cold but she's actually intensely devoted and focused on doing what's right to the exclusion of all else, including her own safety. Her work is the most important thing to her until she met, and secretly married, Colonel Michael Cedars in the middle of the war in Afghanistan. It's in a dark room where they plan for the future and enjoy quiet moments of happiness keeping the war at bay. Their dreams come crashing down as he's severely injured and tries to push her away and deny her existance out of fear. She's a strong-willed woman though who has no intention of giving him up and forces her way back into his life. Her strong outer shell hides her inner turmoil and flashes of PTSD from all the death she's witnessed. I ached to see her moments of weakness as they were so contradictory to how she presents herself. Her latest story puts her right in the thick of a battle at home involving human trafficking that puts her life in jeopardy as well as those around her. Once again Michael's in danger but thankfully they have each other to turn to as the danger is closer than they ever expected. Even though she struggles with survivor's guilt throughout the story she never lets things beat her. No matter how often she's knocked down, she gets right back up to stand by her man and her convictions.<br /><br />Michael Cedars has always been a man in control, so his paralysis is especially frustrating as he now has little control of anything. As a quadriplegic myself I found his feelings believable and the cycle of emotions he goes through towards acceptance realistic. His own body has betrayed him through its weakness that mentally makes him feel like less than a man. He's used to taking care of others but now must be taken care of. At first he pushes Hope away as he wants her to have someone better than him. Through her support and presence though he realizes he's still the man he was, just a slightly different one, that she needs no matter what. He too can admit that he needs her and wants to fulfill those dreams they once made. He accepts her as she is even as others call her reckless. As they reunite in the home she planned for long ago their connection deepens and the hurts they've buried deep inside slowly heal. Love is a healing balm and leads to an immensely satisfying conclusion.<br /><br />Hope and Michael are both flawed characters who sometimes hurt each other in their verbal battles. They love each other wholeheartedly and unconditionally. Their love was vital to them both and as the story progressed they realized how much they'd give up to be together. Their journey towards a HEA was heartbreaking at times but ultimately cheer-inducing. The life of a wheelchair user was presented vividly and accurately and pulled no punches in dealing with the physical, mental, and emotional issues of having a body that's no longer yours to control. The sexual aspects were also dealt with sensitively yet believably. The mystery Hope gets caught up in went on a bit too long but definitely kept me on the edge of my seat guessing whodunit due to its numerous twists and turns. The secondary characters were larger than life with each leaving a lasting impression. This story drew me in completely from page one and kept me immersed in its grittiness until the very satisfying end and I wholeheartedly recommend it to others. This was my first time reading a book from this author but her impressive storytelling has me wanting to come back for more and I look forward to her future releases.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11954938152924392795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17461147204108159640">Wonderful novel, one of the most well written and best developed that I've read in a long time. I'm a war veteran myself and felt the author had an innate understanding of what it's like to </span>
  <span id="freeText17461147204108159640" style="display:none">Wonderful novel, one of the most well written and best developed that I've read in a long time. The characters rung true, the plot pulled me in from the first page, and the ending left me wanting more. I can't think of anything that I didn't like, actually. Very well written--I find it hard to believe anyone would be disappointed by this novel, especially if you like something a bit "more" from a book. I'm a war veteran myself and felt the author had an innate understanding of what it's like to transition back into civilian life. I was a bit surprised at how well she 'nailed it'. This novel has found a special place in my heart. Well done.</span>

<div id="review_1279010072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1279010072" />
    <a title="crashqueen73" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34443574-crashqueen73"><img alt="crashqueen73" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514531550p2/34443574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1279010072?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="crashqueen73" class="user" itemprop="url" name="crashqueen73" href="/user/show/34443574-crashqueen73">crashqueen73</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1279010072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18274372318811096886">This was definitely a decent read. Good solid characters and good sold character development. I think I just wanted more. <br/><br/>It probably sounds shallow but I really don't care too much about story lines that don't aid in the development of the characters or the relationship between the characters and this was one of those for me.<br/><br/>I think I would have liked it better from the war point of view when they were getting together under really difficult circumstances rather than them getting back together </span>
  <span id="freeText18274372318811096886" style="display:none">This was definitely a decent read. Good solid characters and good sold character development. I think I just wanted more. <br /><br />It probably sounds shallow but I really don't care too much about story lines that don't aid in the development of the characters or the relationship between the characters and this was one of those for me.<br /><br />I think I would have liked it better from the war point of view when they were getting together under really difficult circumstances rather than them getting back together once they returned from war. The ending was good where they were working together but the rest of it was just distracting from the actual relationship.<br /><br />I also struggle with lots and lots of characters. Parents, sisters, brothers in law, step sons, best friends, colleagues etc etc. It is very hard to keep up with that many extras along with complicated relationships and life threatening work situations.<br /><br />I personally prefer these complications to have a bearing on the relationship not just an addition to the story. But that is just my opinion. Well written and a solid read. 3 stars because I liked it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18274372318811096886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1453703453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8793088166720611827"><strong>Sexy Thriller</strong><br/><br/>Reckless Endangerment is another sexy and suspenseful thriller from Amber Lea Easton. Recovering from injuries he sustained in an ambush, Colonel Michael Cedars has been unexpectedly transferred from Walter Reed to a facility in Colorado. Investigative journalist Hope Shane has also recently moved to Colorado. She's spent time in a war zone and is hoping for a new start. Known to few is the fact that Hope and Michael have been married for almost a year. <br/><br/>Michael's injuries and PTSD c</span>
  <span id="freeText8793088166720611827" style="display:none"><strong>Sexy Thriller</strong><br /><br />Reckless Endangerment is another sexy and suspenseful thriller from Amber Lea Easton. Recovering from injuries he sustained in an ambush, Colonel Michael Cedars has been unexpectedly transferred from Walter Reed to a facility in Colorado. Investigative journalist Hope Shane has also recently moved to Colorado. She's spent time in a war zone and is hoping for a new start. Known to few is the fact that Hope and Michael have been married for almost a year. <br /><br />Michael's injuries and PTSD cause him to try to push her away but Hope is determined. She also suffers from her own traumatic memories. It's a human trafficking story she's working on that ultimately brings them back together. But Hope's involvement jeopardizes everyone she loves.<br /><br />This is an exciting, suspenseful book but at its core, it's a heart-wrenching love story. I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8793088166720611827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cBAHXjNMJqS2m0CGcJB+3utA9lzwzLQqbVrxyQUQSyO2i0ba/OvQwDVYpEnRwyNWNtPKC0Vq1bZftAxipCH9RA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h/CRnYTth9ur/N9HZ9kv413lUTJ1cuT2u95irZvpQelBa9AZS0pxvyg/O4jGinJrgHZtZcDUhWqJMJ8GOtj3jg==')})
  }
//]]>

Upon arrival, s<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5007801690193726982\" style=\"display:none\">A tale of family, brotherhood, and the healing power of love\n\nAfter the tragic death of her husband, Aven Norgaard is beckoned to give up her life in Norway to become a housekeeper in the rugged hills of nineteenth-century Appalachia. Upon arrival, she finds herself in the home of her late husband’s cousins—three brothers who make a living by brewing hard cider on their three-hundred-acre farm. Yet even as a stranger in a foreign land, Aven has hope to build a new life in this tight-knit family.\n\nBut her unassuming beauty disrupts the bond between the brothers. The youngest two both desire her hand, and Aven is caught in the middle, unsure where—and whether—to offer her affection. While Haakon is bold and passionate, it is Thor who casts the greatest spell upon her. Though Deaf, mute, and dependent on hard drink to cope with his silent pain, Thor possesses a sobering strength.\n\nAs autumn ushers in the apple harvest, the rift between Thor and Haakon deepens and Aven faces a choice that risks hearts. Will two brothers\' longing for her quiet spirit tear apart a family? Can she find a tender belonging in this remote, rugged, and unfamiliar place?\n\nA haunting tale of struggle and redemption, Sons of Blackbird Mountain is a portrait of grace in a world where the       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5366587.Amber_Lea_Easton">About Amber Lea Easton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5366587.Amber_Lea_Easton"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1366763564p3/5366587.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5366587.Amber_Lea_Easton">Amber Lea Easton
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11450073014060975202"> Amber Lea Easton is a multi-published fiction and nonfiction author. For twenty years, she's worked in the fields of journalism and advertising with a brief detour into the financial industry. Although she holds a BA in Communications & Journalism, she is a perpetual student of life who enjoys taking classes on a wide variety of subjects when time allows.<br/><br/> Smart is sexy, according to Easton, which</span>
  <span id="freeText11450073014060975202" style="display:none"> Amber Lea Easton is a multi-published fiction and nonfiction author. For twenty years, she's worked in the fields of journalism and advertising with a brief detour into the financial industry. Although she holds a BA in Communications &amp; Journalism, she is a perpetual student of life who enjoys taking classes on a wide variety of subjects when time allows.<br /><br /> Smart is sexy, according to Easton, which is why she writes about strong female characters who have their flaws and challenges but ultimately persevere. She currently has three romantic suspense novels out in the world, Kiss Me Slowly, Riptide and Reckless Endangerment, and a contemporary romance novella, Anonymity. <br /><br />Her memoir, Free Fall, released on September 1, 2013, and is dedicated to suicide prevention, awareness, and helping others navigate the dark journey of grief. <br /><br /> In addition to fiction writing, Easton also edits and freelances. She also speaks on subjects ranging from writing to widowhood. Some of her videos on romance writing have appeared on the international Writers &amp; Authors television network. Current radio appearances are linked via this site and her blog Kisses, Caresses &amp; Whispers in the Night.<br /><br /> Easton currently lives with her two teenagers in the Colorado Rocky Mountains where she gives thanks daily for the gorgeous view outside her window. She finds inspiration from traveling, the people she meets, nature and life’s twists and turns. At the end of the day, as long as she's writing, she considers herself to be simply "a lucky lady liv'n the dream."﻿</span>
  <a data-text-id="11450073014060975202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
